< name>
John Hanken<//name>
<Date>1544909196877< /Date><rating>5</rating>< Text>
This is my "go to" spot in the North Tahoe area. At Sugarbowl, you can elect to go to the Village Lodge Hotel, it's a great experience, you ride the Gondola to the only snow-bound village in Tahoe, and that Lodge has tons of history, good food and drink, a great pro shop and is very cool. But if you want to hit it hard and early, the Judah Lodge has the best ingress/egress, a great place to get your food bag on, you've got Finish Line that will edge and wax your board/stix for a reasonable price while you are eating or wait for the lifts to open. This place is the most accessible and fun place to ski for my time/money. The people are great too!< /Text>

< review>
I love this park. It has big open fields for flying kites or volleyball or soccer. It also has basketball courts, a nice playground, and lots of swings. The best part is that the baby swings are in the shade during the hotter hours.

I almost forgot the water park! It's on an automatic timer that starts every 10 minutes and the park is open for all of the hot months.

This park is fantastic.< /review>

This park is good to spend time as a family. This park has a BBQ area, water area for the kids to get wet and have lots of fun in, a play area with slides and swings, lots of grass to play in, and places to sit while you enjoy watching your kids have fun. The cons of this park there is no bathrooms, the place is a bit rundown, and spray paint on some of the equipment. But if you can overlook those this is a fun park.

If this is not the park for you there is a better park with a water area in Olivehurst called Eufey Wood Spray Park.<//review>

<Pictures>None</Pictures><Rating>4</Rating>< username>
Marco Paganini<//username>
<user_id>104042685529602206608< /user_id>< text>
The Hole-in-the-Wall Information Center is located inside the Hole-in-the-Wall campground, which I believe will be what most people are interested in.

This is a nice campground in the desert with a lot of campsites for RVs. It features the usual amenities like fire pits, communal pit bathrooms, manual water pumps and even an RV dump station. There are no water or power hookups. This campground is very popular and it's a good idea to arrive with some extra hours of sunlight in case you can't find a spot.

There are excellent walking trails around, including the infamous "Ring Loop Trail" where you get to climb (or descend) Banshee Canyon using metal hoops. I'd definitely recommend giving it a try.

The only somewhat negative aspect of this campground is its popularity -- you may not find the solitude you're looking for in the desert.

When arriving, I'd suggest taking I40, Essex Road, and then Black Canyon Road going north up to the campground entrance. The alternative (Black Canyon Road south from Cedar Canyon Road) can be long and rough if you're driving a large vehicle.</text>

Went here in the morning on a Saturday at 9:55am right before opening and was the first customer of the day! The shop was very clean with fresh air and tall ceilings. I felt safe right away as Ruby greeted me and took my temperature and had her mask on properly (covering the nose). Everything in there felt very clean and sanitary.

<Text>The smell. The flys. The dangerously full latrines. The overflowing garbage dumpsters. The horror!

Look, I get that these are *latrines* in the middle of the Mojave Desert. I get that plumbing and electric don't exist here. I didn't expect luxury accommodations. But, I would expect that this rest area would at least be serviced occasionally.

We were there in the middle of the week, not a busy Saturday. The dumpsters were a safety and health hazard, with all manner of trash overflowing and pooling around the ground outside the dumpsters.

Each and every latrine was dangerously full - nearly to the brim on each and every one. The smell that was emitting from them about knocked you out the second you opened the car door. You couldn't even close the door when you were in the stall using the latrine for fear the noxious fumes would knock you out. I don't even remember if there was toilet paper or hand sanitizer. I was too busy racing back to the car!

I'm hope they create and adhere to some kind of maintenance schedule for this rest area. If they already have one in place, I hope they revise it.<//Text>< Pictures>
